   <div class="wrapper">
    <div class="col span_10 clr span_content" id="content">
     <article class="post">
      <header class="posthead">
       <h2 class="posttitle">
        Old Fashioned Blueberry Pudding with Rosewater Sauce (GIVEAWAY)
       </h2>
       <div class="postmeta">
        <em>
         posted by
        </em>
        Sommer 
        <a href="http://www.aspicyperspective.com/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway/#comments">
         228 comments 
        </a>
       </div>
      </header>
      <div class="shareaholic-canvas" data-app="share_buttons" data-app-id="17464635" data-link="http://www.aspicyperspective.com/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway/" data-summary="" data-title="Old Fashioned Blueberry Pudding with Rosewater Sauce (GIVEAWAY)">
      </div>
      <p style="text-align: center;">
       <a href="http://aspicyperspective.com/2011/10/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway.html/img_0126" rel="attachment wp-att-7513">
        <img alt="Old Fashioned Blueberry Pudding with Rosewater Sauce" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-7513" height="420" src="http://aspicyperspective.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/IMG_0126.jpg" title="old-fashoned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce.jpg" width="420"/>
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       This post will strike some of you with giddy jubilation and reminiscing while others will roll their eyes when I confess Im writing about
       <strong>
        Little House on the Prairie
       </strong>
       today. For the latter, DONT GO! Youll miss out on an incredible
       <em>
        <strong>
         Old Fashioned Blueberry Pudding with Rosewater Sauce
        </strong>
       </em>
       <strong>
        <em>
         Recipe
        </em>
       </strong>
       and a gorgeous Villeroy &amp; Boch GIVEAWAY. I promise its worth it to bear my ramblings for a few moments.
      </p>
      <p>
       <span id="more-6936">
       </span>
       This summer I was determined to read my children the entire
       <a href="http://www.littlehousebooks.com/">
        <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
         Little House Series
        </span>
       </a>
       from
       <a href="http://www.lauraingallswilder.com/">
        Laura Ingalls Wilder
       </a>
       . I remember being captivated by the books as a child and wanted to see my little ones eyes light up with Lauras antics.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="http://aspicyperspective.com/2011/10/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway.html/little-house-m" rel="attachment wp-att-6950">
        <img alt="Little House Books" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-6950" height="960" src="http://aspicyperspective.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/Little-House-M.jpg" title="little-house-books.jpg" width="600"/>
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
        The Little House on the Prairie
       </span>
       books are a remarkable, and deliciously descriptive, historical tail of the Ingalls clan, a pioneer family in the 1800s that moved from Wisconsin, to Oklahoma Indian Territory, back north to Minnesota and finally to South Dakota, all by covered wagon. Although the books are categorized as historical fiction due to Lauras embellishments, most of the astonishing accounts are true.
      </p>
      <p>
       In modern day, its hard to fully grasp the lifestyle and mindset of an early American pioneer family. To read these books, one would think Laura was completely obsessed with food. Not in the way WE obsess over carbs, gourmet chocolates, or local produce,
       <em>
        but engrossed with food for survival
       </em>
       . From hunting to foraging, fishing, berrying, farming, cooking, freezing, salt-preserving, drying, and canning nourishment CONSUMED them. Thats not to say they didnt enjoy their meals. However, sustenance was extremely valuable. Something held with such importance was worth taking the time to document.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="http://aspicyperspective.com/2011/10/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway.html/img_0045" rel="attachment wp-att-7509">
        <img alt="Blueberry Pudding" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-7509" height="900" src="http://aspicyperspective.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/IMG_0045.jpg" title="blueberry-pudding.jpg" width="600"/>
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       Not only does this mouthwatering narrative go into great detail describing the preparation of daily meals, Laura weaves a feast for the senses with smells, crackling sounds, and hearty dishes your dying to try.
      </p>
      <p>
       <em>
        Ma made vanity cakes. She made them with beaten eggs and white flour. She dropped them into a kettle of sizzling fat. Each one came up bobbling, and floated till it turned itself over, lifting up its honey-brown puffy bottom. Then it swelled underneath till it was round and Ma lifted it out with a fork The cakes were not sweet, but they were rich and crisp, and hollow on the inside. Each one was like a great bubble. The crisp bits of it melted on the tongue They said they had never tasted anything so good and they asked Ma what they were. Vanity Cakes, said Ma. Because they are all puffed up, like vanity, with nothing solid inside.
       </em>
       ~
       <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
        On The Banks Of Plum Creek
       </span>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="http://aspicyperspective.com/2011/10/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway.html/img_0057" rel="attachment wp-att-7510">
        <img alt="How To Make Blueberry Pudding" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-7510" height="911" src="http://aspicyperspective.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/IMG_0057.jpg" title="how-to-make-blueberry-pudding.jpg" width="600"/>
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       <em>
        Fathers spoon cut deep into the chicken-pie; he scooped out big pieces of thick crust and turned up their fluffy yellow under-sides on the plate. He poured gravy over them; he dipped up big pieces of tender chicken, dark meat and white meat sliding from the bones. He added a mound of baked beans and topped it with a quivering slice of pork fat. At the edge of the plate he piled dark-red beet pickles. And he handed the plate to Almanzo. Silently Almanzo ate it all.
       </em>
       ~
       <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
        Farmer Boy
       </span>
      </p>
      <p>
       See what a mean? I drooled through the entire series.
       <strong>
        The Little House Books are a MUST-READ for food lovers of all ages.
       </strong>
       (Put it on your electronic reader, I wont tell.)
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="http://aspicyperspective.com/2011/10/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway.html/img_0067" rel="attachment wp-att-7511">
        <img alt="Rosewater Sauce" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-7511" height="900" src="http://aspicyperspective.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/IMG_0067.jpg" title="rosewater-sauce.jpg" width="600"/>
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       Needless to say, I HAD to buy
       <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
        The Little House Cookbook
       </span>
       . What fun its been flipping through the pages of frontier recipes; dishes cooked over open flame and churned to perfection.
      </p>
      <p>
       This
       <em>
        <strong>
         Old Fashioned Blueberry Pudding with Rosewater Sauce
        </strong>
       </em>
       is inspired by the blueberry pudding Almanzos mother made after a long day of berrying in the book
       <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
        Farmer Boy
       </span>
       . I didnt use the exact recipe in the cookbook, because it was developed before most homes had reliable ovens. Therefore, it was cooked in a tin can submerged in water on the stovetop.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="http://aspicyperspective.com/2011/10/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway.html/img_0091" rel="attachment wp-att-7512">
        <img alt="Old Fashioned Blueberry Pudding" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-7512" height="850" src="http://aspicyperspective.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/IMG_0091.jpg" title="old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding.jpg" width="600"/>
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       This oven-friendly pudding is not a
       <a href="http://www.joythebaker.com/blog/2008/04/old-fashioned-chocolate-pudding/">
        custard
       </a>
       as we think of pudding; its more of a hefty cake that you scoop up with a spoon. Its dense, hearty and not overly sweet, with a cornbread-like consistency. A pudding of this variety would have been served with milk, or a sweet sauce, poured over the top to moisten it.
      </p>
      <p>
       Although rosewater is now generally considered a middle-eastern ingredient, it was widely used for flavoring in early American days, because people could
       <a href="http://www.care2.com/greenliving/rose-water-how-to-make-your-own.html">
        make it easily
       </a>
       from wild roses.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="http://aspicyperspective.com/2011/10/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway.html/img_0105" rel="attachment wp-att-6960">
        <img alt="" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-6960" height="860" src="http://aspicyperspective.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/IMG_0105.jpg" title="IMG_0105" width="600"/>
       </a>
      </p>
      <p>
       Admittedly, Ive tried rosewater in several dishes and beverages and havent been impressed, but the combination of rosewater, nutmeg and butter in this silky sauce is exquisite. Poured over the rustic and tart blueberry pudding
       <em>
        sigh
       </em>
       . I honestly could not get enough of it!
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="http://aspicyperspective.com/2011/10/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway.html/img_0124" rel="attachment wp-att-6953">
        <img alt="" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-6953" height="855" src="http://aspicyperspective.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/IMG_0124.jpg" title="IMG_0124" width="600"/>
       </a>
      </p>
      <div class="recipe" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Recipe">
       <meta content="http://www.aspicyperspective.com/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway" itemprop="url"/>
       <img align="right" class="photo nopin" itemprop="image" nopin="nopin" src="http://xnjm5arbt0-flywheel.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/IMG_0126-210x210.jpg"/>
       <span itemprop="name">
        <h2 class="fn">
         Old Fashioned Blueberry Pudding with Rosewater Sauce
        </h2>
       </span>
       <div class="time">
        <p>
         <strong>
          Yield:
         </strong>
         <span itemprop="recipeYield">
          12 servings
         </span>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          Prep Time:
         </strong>
         <meta content="PT15M" itemprop="prepTime"/>
         15 minutes
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          Cook Time:
         </strong>
         <meta content="PT40-60M" itemprop="cookTime"/>
         40-60 minutes
        </p>
       </div>
       <div class="printbutton">
        <a class="print" href="http://www.aspicyperspective.com/old-fashioned-blueberry-pudding-with-rosewater-sauce-giveaway/print/" title="Print Recipe">
         Print Recipe
        </a>
       </div>
       <h3 id="ingredients">
        Ingredients:
       </h3>
       <div class="ingredients">
        <p>
         For the Old Fashioned Blueberry Pudding:
         <br/>
         5 Tb. butter, divided
         <br/>
         3  cups all-purpose flour
         <br/>
         1  cups granulated sugar
         <br/>
         5 tsp. baking powder
         <br/>
         1 tsp. cinnamon
         <br/>
          tsp. salt
         <br/>
         1 2/3 cups milk
         <br/>
         2 eggs
         <br/>
         2 pints blueberries
        </p>
        <p>
         For the Rosewater Sauce:
         <br/>
         2 cups powdered sugar
         <br/>
         1 pinch salt
         <br/>
          tsp. nutmeg
         <br/>
         4 Tb. rosewater
         <br/>
         6 Tb. melted butter
         <br/>
          tsp. vanilla extract
        </p>
       </div>
       <h3 id="directions">
        Directions:
       </h3>
       <div class="instructions">
        <span itemprop="recipeInstructions">
         <p>
          Preheat the oven to 400 degree F. Use 2 Tb. butter to grease a large baking dish. (9X13 or a smaller deeper dish.)
         </p>
         <p>
          In a large bowl, whisk together the flour, sugar, baking powder, cinnamon and salt. In a separate bowl, whisk the milk, remaining butter (melted) and 2 eggs.
         </p>
         <p>
          Mix the wet mixture into the dry mixture until well combined. Then stir in the blueberries, withholding a large handful for the top.
         </p>
         <p>
          Pour the batter into the baking dish and sprinkle the remaining berries over the top. Bake 40-60 minutes (depending on the depth of the dish) until a toothpick comes out clean.
         </p>
         <p>
          Meanwhile, whisk together the ingredients for the rosewater sauce and set aside.
         </p>
         <p>
          To serve, scoop the warm pudding onto plates and drizzle with rosewater sauce.
         </p>
        </span>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="subrecipe">
       <p>
        <em>
         Making this recipe?
        </em>
        Why not take a quick shot and share it
        <a href="http://instagram.com/spicyperspectiv" target="_blank">
         on Instagram
        </a>
        ! Make sure to tag it
        <strong>
         #ASpicyPerspective
        </strong>
        so we can see what you're cooking!
       </p>
      </div>

   <script type="text/javascript">
    jQuery(document).ready(function() {
	    var offset = 220;
	    var duration = 500;
	    jQuery(window).scroll(function() {
	        if (jQuery(this).scrollTop() &gt; offset) {
	            jQuery('.top').fadeIn(duration);
	        } else {
	            jQuery('.top').fadeOut(duration);
	        }
	    });
	    
	    jQuery('.top').click(function(event) {
	        event.preventDefault();
	        jQuery('html, body').animate({scrollTop: 0}, duration);
	        return false;
	    })
	});
   </script>
